\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\subsubsection*{template$<$class T, class Allocator = std\+::allocator$<$\+T$>$, Layout\+Management layout = Optimize\+For\+Speed, unsigned Min\+B\+Size = S\+E\+Q\+\_\+\+M\+I\+N\+\_\+\+B\+U\+C\+K\+E\+T\+\_\+\+S\+I\+Z\+E(\+T), unsigned Max\+B\+Size = S\+E\+Q\+\_\+\+M\+A\+X\+\_\+\+B\+U\+C\+K\+E\+T\+\_\+\+S\+I\+ZE, class Find\+B\+Size = detail\+::\+Find\+Bucket\+Size$<$\+T$>$, bool Store\+Back\+Values = false, class Value\+Compare = detail\+::\+Null\+Value\+Compare$<$\+T$>$$>$\newline
class seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector$<$ T, Allocator, layout, Min\+B\+Size, Max\+B\+Size, Find\+B\+Size, Store\+Back\+Values, Value\+Compare $>$}

\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} is a std\+\_\+deque like container implemented as a tiered-\/vector. 


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & value type \\
\hline
{\em Allocator} & allocator type \\
\hline
{\em layout} & memory layout \\
\hline
{\em Min\+B\+Size} & minimum bucket size, depends on the value\+\_\+type size \\
\hline
{\em Max\+B\+Size} & maximum bucket size \\
\hline
{\em Find\+B\+Size} & struct used to find the bucket size for a given \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{tiered\+\_\+vector}} size \\
\hline
{\em Value\+Compare} & internal use only\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} is a random-\/access, bucket based container providing a similar interface to std\+\_\+deque. Its internals are however very different as it is implemented as a \href{http://cs.brown.edu/cgc/jdsl/papers/tiered-vector.pdf}{\texttt{ tiered vector}}. Instead of maintaining a vector of fixed size buckets, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} uses a bucket size close to sqrt(size()). The bucket size is always a power of 2 for fast division and modulo. Furtheremore, the bucket is not a linear buffer but is instead implemented as a circular buffer. This allows a complexity of O(sqrt(\+N)) for insertion and deletion in the middle of the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{tiered\+\_\+vector}} instead of O(\+N) for std\+\_\+deque. Inserting and deleting elements at both ends is still O(1).

\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} internally uses \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1devector}{seq\+::devector}} to store the buckets. \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} is used as the backend container for \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1flat__set}{seq\+::flat\+\_\+set}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1flat__map}{seq\+::flat\+\_\+map}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1flat__multiset}{seq\+::flat\+\_\+multiset}} and \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1flat__multimap}{seq\+::flat\+\_\+multimap}}.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md48}{}\doxysubsubsection{Interface}\label{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md48}
\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} interface is the same as std\+\_\+deque, with the additional members\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a8de3daa2bab53b24154ba50a95e22d67}{for\+\_\+each()}} providing a faster way to walk through the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{tiered\+\_\+vector}} than iterators,
\item \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_addb047905aa75bf953571fffe2d164a6}{resize\+\_\+front()}} to resize the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{tiered\+\_\+vector}} from the front instead of the back of the container,
\end{DoxyItemize}\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md49}{}\doxysubsubsection{Bucket managment}\label{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md49}
The \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} maintains internally an array of circular buffers (or buckets). At any moment, all buckets have the same size which is a power of 2. At container initialization, the bucket size is given by template parameter {\itshape Min\+B\+Size} which is, by default, between 64 and 8 depending on value\+\_\+type size. Whenever \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} grows (through \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_ad80f18ac21202413a8ef61e89079f6c4}{push\+\_\+back()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a312a16493aa0b324786ed30ec951be34}{push\+\_\+front()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a12ce048bdca3058607f68a50b94369e9}{insert()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a9f360b40b18a28158342a20dedb53094}{resize()}} ...), the new bucket size is computed using the template parameter {\itshape Find\+B\+Size}. {\itshape Find\+B\+Size} must provide the member 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keywordtype}{unsigned}  FindBSize::operator() (\textcolor{keywordtype}{size\_t} \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a4703b4f2463d0d19f6313f6b1fb81edb}{size}}, \textcolor{keywordtype}{unsigned} MinBSize, \textcolor{keywordtype}{unsigned} MaxBSize) \textcolor{keyword}{const} noexcept ;}
\end{DoxyCode}
 returning the new bucket size based on the container size, the minimum and maximum bucket size. Default implementation returns a value close to sqrt(size()) rounded up to the next power of 2.

If the new bucket size is different than the current one, new buckets are created and elements from the old buckets are moved to the new ones. This has the practical consequence to {\bfseries{ invalidate all iterators and references on growing or shrinking }}, as opposed to std\+\_\+deque which maintains references when inserting/deleting at both ends.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md50}{}\doxysubsubsection{Inserting and deleting elements}\label{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md50}
Inserting or deleting elements at the back or the front behaves the same way as for std\+\_\+deque, except if the bucket size is updated (as explained above).

Inerting an element in the middle of \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} follows these steps\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item The bucket index and the element position within the bucket are first computed
\item The back element of the bucket is extracted and removed from the bucket
\item The new element is inserted at the right position. Since the bucket is implemented as a dense circular buffer, at most half of the bucket elements must be moved (toward the left or the right, whichever is the shortest path)
\item The back value that was previously removed is inserted at the front of the next bucket
\item The next bucket back value is extracted and inserted at the front of the following bucket
\item ....
\item And so forth until we reach the last bucket.
\end{DoxyItemize}

This operation of {\itshape insert front/pop back} is very fast on a circular buffer as it involves only two element moves and shifting the begin index of the buffer. If the bucket size is exactly sqrt(size()), inserting an element in the middle performs in O(sqrt(\+N)) as it involves as many element moves within a single bucket than between buckets.

In practice the buckets size should be greater than sqrt(size()) as moving elements within a bucket is much faster than between buckets due to cache locality.

Note that, depending on the insertion location, elements can be shifted toward the front bucket instead of the back one if this is the shortest path. This practically divides by 2 (on average) the number of moved elements.

Erasing an element in the middle follows the exact same logic.

Note that inserting/removing relocatable types (where \mbox{\hyperlink{structseq_1_1is__relocatable_a9bc3104d310961a601c2185957f846ad}{seq\+::is\+\_\+relocatable$<$\+T$>$\+::value}} is true) is faster than for other types.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md51}{}\doxysubsubsection{Exception guarantee}\label{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md51}
All insertion/deletion operations on a \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} are much more complex than for a std\+\_\+deque. Especially, each operation might change the bucket size, and therefore trigger the allocation of new buckets plus moving all elements within the new buckets.

Although possible, providing strong exception guarantee on \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} operations would have added a very complex layer hurting its performances. Therefore, all \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} operations only provide {\bfseries{basic exception guarantee}}.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md52}{}\doxysubsubsection{Iterators and references invalidation}\label{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md52}
As explained above, all \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} operations invalidate iterators and references, except for swapping two \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}}.

The only exception is when providing a minimum bucket size ({\itshape Min\+B\+Size}) equals to the maximum bucket size ({\itshape Max\+B\+Size}). In this case, inserting/deleting elements will {\itshape never} change the bucket size and move all elements within new buckets. This affects the members \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_aaf44e867eb42ca875b9e1b821da0adf9}{emplace\+\_\+back()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_ad80f18ac21202413a8ef61e89079f6c4}{push\+\_\+back()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_ad46f6000255d198a1bd02b96b5d4fcb8}{emplace\+\_\+front()}} and \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a312a16493aa0b324786ed30ec951be34}{push\+\_\+front()}} that provide the same invalidation rules as for std\+\_\+deque.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md53}{}\doxysubsubsection{Memory layout}\label{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md53}
If the {\itshape layout} template parameter is {\itshape Optimize\+For\+Memory}, each bucket is independantly allocated using the provided allocator, and the buckets are automatically deallocated when empty.

When using the {\itshape Optimize\+For\+Speed} flag, the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} will use a memory pool to allocate several buckets at once, still using the provided allocator. The memory pool uses a growing strategy to allocate more and more buckets based on a growth factor (S\+E\+Q\+\_\+\+G\+R\+O\+W\+\_\+\+F\+A\+C\+T\+OR define, defaulting to 1.\+6). Whenever the bucket size changes, memory chunks used to store the previous buckets are kept as long as they are big enough to hold buckets of the new size. This avoid a lot of unnecessary allocations when continuously extending the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}}. The memory pool makes insertion tipically 50\% faster (depending on value\+\_\+type size) than the default allocation strategy, but will consume slightly more memory.

With {\itshape Optimize\+For\+Speed} flag, the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{tiered\+\_\+vector}} will almost never release memory, except on calls to \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a381dfa730a7fed2835c671d1173e0df4}{shrink\+\_\+to\+\_\+fit()}}.\hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md54}{}\doxysubsubsection{Performances}\label{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_autotoc_md54}
\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} was optimized to match libc++ std\+\_\+deque performances as close as possible. My benchmarhs shows that all members are actually faster than libc++ std\+\_\+deque, except for \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_ad80f18ac21202413a8ef61e89079f6c4}{push\+\_\+back()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a312a16493aa0b324786ed30ec951be34}{push\+\_\+front()}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_aebbfb66c36a48f7c68e8ee6a36fedbfa}{pop\+\_\+back()}} and \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a5777b3ade76286515ffe15a3c05bf770}{pop\+\_\+front()}} which are slightly slower due to the need to move all elements when the bucket size changes. This can be alievated by the {\itshape Optimize\+For\+Speed} flag that makes both operations faster than their std\+\_\+deque counterparts.

Usually, iterating through a \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} is faster than through a std\+\_\+deque. The random-\/access \#operator\mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}(size\+\_\+t) is also faster. Making a lot of random access based on iterators can be slightly slower with \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} depending on the use case. For instance, sorting a \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} is slower than sorting a std\+\_\+deque.

Inserting/deleting single elements on a \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}} is several order of magnitudes faster than std\+\_\+deque due to the tiered-\/vector implementation.

The standard conlusion is\+: you should always benchmark with your own use cases.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a28487b5e58bbf62c7358dd7dfa9906af}\label{classseq_1_1tiered__vector_a28487b5e58bbf62c7358dd7dfa9906af}} 
\index{seq::tiered\_vector$<$ T, Allocator, layout, MinBSize, MaxBSize, FindBSize, StoreBackValues, ValueCompare $>$@{seq::tiered\_vector$<$ T, Allocator, layout, MinBSize, MaxBSize, FindBSize, StoreBackValues, ValueCompare $>$}!const\_reference@{const\_reference}}
\index{const\_reference@{const\_reference}!seq::tiered\_vector$<$ T, Allocator, layout, MinBSize, MaxBSize, FindBSize, StoreBackValues, ValueCompare $>$@{seq::tiered\_vector$<$ T, Allocator, layout, MinBSize, MaxBSize, FindBSize, StoreBackValues, ValueCompare $>$}}

Resizes the container to contain count elements. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em count} & new size of the container If the current size is greater than count, the container is reduced to its first count elements. If the current size is less than count, additional default-\/inserted elements are appended. Basic exception guarantee. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

Resizes the container to contain count elements. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em count} & new size of the container \\
\hline
{\em value} & the value to initialize the new elements with If the current size is greater than count, the container is reduced to its first count elements. If the current size is less than count, additional copies of value are appended. Basic exception guarantee. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

Release all unused memory, and move the \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{tiered\+\_\+vector}} content to the smallest possible storage. This function only makes sense for {\itshape Optimize\+For\+Speed} flag. Invalidate all iterators and references.

void \mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{seq\+::tiered\+\_\+vector}}$<$ T, Allocator, layout, Min\+B\+Size, Max\+B\+Size, Find\+B\+Size, Store\+Back\+Values, Value\+Compare $>$\+::swap (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classseq_1_1tiered__vector}{tiered\+\_\+vector}}$<$ T, Allocator, layout, Min\+B\+Size, Max\+B\+Size, Find\+B\+Size, Store\+Back\+Values, Value\+Compare $>$ \&}]{other }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [noexcept]}}



Exchanges the contents of the container with those of other. Does not invoke any move, copy, or swap operations on individual elements. 


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em other} & other sequence to swap with All iterators and references remain valid. An iterator holding the past-\/the-\/end value in this container will refer to the other container after the operation. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
